<p><b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">Driving</b> safety experts predict that once driverless technology has been fully developed, <a href="/wiki/Traffic_collision" title="Traffic collision">traffic collisions</a> (and <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology_of_motor_vehicle_collisions" title="Epidemiology of motor vehicle collisions">resulting deaths and injuries</a> and costs) caused by <a href="/wiki/Human_error" title="Human error">human error</a>, such as delayed <a href="/wiki/Stopping_sight_distance" title="Stopping sight distance">reaction time</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tail_gating" class="mw-redirect" title="Tail gating">tailgating</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rubbernecking" title="Rubbernecking">rubbernecking</a>, and other forms of <a href="/wiki/Distracted_driving" title="Distracted driving">distracted</a> or <a href="/wiki/Aggressive_driving" title="Aggressive driving">aggressive <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b></a> should be substantially reduced.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-morgan_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morgan-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theenergycollective.com_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theenergycollective.com-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Whitwam_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whitwam-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt-2011_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-2011-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> If 90% of <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> in the US became <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b>, for example, an estimated 25,000 lives would be saved annually.<sup id="cite_ref-Rojas_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rojas-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to motorist website "TheDrive.com" operated by <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine, none of the <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> safety experts they were able to contact were able to rank <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> under an autopilot system at the time (2017) as having achieved a greater level of safety than traditional fully hands-on <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b>, so the degree to which these benefits asserted by proponents will manifest in practice cannot be assessed.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Confounding factors that could reduce the net effect on safety may include unexpected interactions between humans and partly or fully automated vehicles, or between different types of vehicle system; complications at the boundaries of functionality at each automation level (such as handover when the vehicle reaches the limit of its capacity); the effect of the bugs and flaws that inevitably occur in complex interdependent software systems; sensor or data shortcomings; and successful compromise by malicious interveners. Security problems include what an autonomous car might do if summoned to pick up the owner but another person attempts entry, what happens if someone tries to break in to the car, and what happens if someone attacks the occupants, for example by exchanging gunfire.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To help reduce the possibility of these confounding factors, some companies have begun to <a href="/wiki/Open-source" class="mw-redirect" title="Open-source">open-source</a> parts of their driverless systems. <a href="/wiki/Udacity" title="Udacity">Udacity</a> for instance is developing an open-source <a href="/wiki/Software_stack" class="mw-redirect" title="Software stack">software stack</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> and some companies are having similar approaches.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (August 2019)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> believe that once automation in vehicles reaches higher levels and becomes reliable, drivers will pay less attention to the road.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Research shows that drivers in automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> react later when they have to intervene in a critical situation, compared to if they were <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> manually.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Depending on the capabilities of automated vehicles and the frequency with which human intervention is needed, this may counteract any increase in safety, as compared to all-human <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b>, that may be delivered by other factors.
</p><p>A potential side effect of decreasing car accidents is reducing the supply of <a href="/wiki/Organ_donation" title="Organ donation">organs for donation</a>. In the US, for example, 13% of the organ donation supply comes from car crash victims.<sup id="cite_ref-Rojas_111-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rojas-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Welfare">Welfare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Welfare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> could reduce <a href="/wiki/Labor_costs" class="mw-redirect" title="Labor costs">labor costs</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Light_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Light-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> relieve travelers from <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> and navigation chores, thereby replacing behind-the-wheel commuting hours with more time for leisure or work;<sup id="cite_ref-morgan_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morgan-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt-2011_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-2011-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> and also would lift constraints on occupant ability to drive, distracted and <a href="/wiki/Texting_while_driving" title="Texting while driving">texting while <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b></a>, <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_intoxication" title="Alcohol intoxication">intoxicated</a>, prone to <a href="/wiki/Seizures" class="mw-redirect" title="Seizures">seizures</a>, or otherwise impaired.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tooOld_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tooOld-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> For the young, the <a href="/wiki/Elderly" class="mw-redirect" title="Elderly">elderly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disability" title="Disability">people with disabilities</a>, and low-income citizens, automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> could provide enhanced <a href="/wiki/Mobility_aid" title="Mobility aid">mobility</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RAND_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAND-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The removal of the steering wheel—along with the remaining driver interface and the requirement for any occupant to assume a forward-facing position—would give the interior of the cabin greater ergonomic flexibility. Large vehicles, such as motorhomes, would attain appreciably enhanced ease of use.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traffic">Traffic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Additional advantages could include higher <a href="/wiki/Speed_limit" title="Speed limit">speed limits</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> smoother rides;<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> and increased roadway capacity; and minimized <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">traffic congestion</a>, due to decreased need for safety gaps and higher speeds.<sup id="cite_ref-gridlock_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gridlock-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-humanIrrelevance_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-humanIrrelevance-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Currently, maximum <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highway" title="Controlled-access highway">controlled-access highway</a> throughput or capacity according to the US <a href="/wiki/Highway_Capacity_Manual" title="Highway Capacity Manual">Highway Capacity Manual</a> is about 2,200 passenger vehicles per hour per lane, with about 5% of the available road space is taken up by <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b>. One study estimated that automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> could increase capacity by 273% (≈8,200 <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> per hour per lane). The study also estimated that with 100% connected vehicles using vehicle-to-vehicle communication, capacity could reach 12,000 passenger vehicles per hour (up 545% from 2,200&#160;pc/h per lane) traveling safely at 120&#160;km/h (75&#160;mph) with a following gap of about 6&#160;m (20&#160;ft) of each other. Human drivers at highway speeds keep between 40 to 50&#160;m (130 to 160&#160;ft) away from the vehicle in front. These increases in highway capacity could have a significant impact in traffic congestion, particularly in urban areas, and even effectively end highway congestion in some places.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> The ability for authorities to manage <a href="/wiki/Traffic_flow" title="Traffic flow">traffic flow</a> would increase, given the extra data and <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> behavior predictability<sup id="cite_ref-Gibson_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gibson-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> combined with less need for <a href="/wiki/Traffic_police" title="Traffic police">traffic police</a> and even <a href="/wiki/Road_signage" class="mw-redirect" title="Road signage">road signage</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_effects">Economic effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Economic effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Safer <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> is expected to reduce the costs of <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_insurance" title="Vehicle insurance">vehicle insurance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Light_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Light-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (November 2019)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Lives saved by averting automobile crashes in the US has been valued at more than $200 billion annually.<sup id="cite_ref-Rojas_111-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rojas-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A direct impact of widespread adoption of automated vehicles is the loss of <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b>-related jobs in the road transport industry.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Light_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Light-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> There could be resistance from professional drivers and unions who are threatened by job losses.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> In addition, there could be job losses in public transit services and crash repair shops. The automobile insurance industry might suffer as the technology makes certain aspects of these occupations obsolete.<sup id="cite_ref-RAND_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAND-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> A frequently cited paper by Michael Osborne and <a href="/wiki/Carl_Benedikt_Frey" title="Carl Benedikt Frey">Carl Benedikt Frey</a> found that automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> would make many jobs redundant.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_and_environmental_impacts">Energy and environmental impacts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Energy and environmental impacts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Vehicle automation can improve <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_automobiles" title="Fuel economy in automobiles">fuel economy</a> of the car by optimizing the drive cycle.<sup id="cite_ref-EEICAV_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEICAV-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Reduced traffic congestion and the improvements in traffic flow due to widespread use of automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> will translate into higher <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_automobiles" title="Fuel economy in automobiles">fuel efficiency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> will be able to accelerate and brake more efficiently, meaning higher fuel economy from reducing wasted energy typically associated with inefficient changes to speed. However, the improvement in vehicle energy efficiency does not necessarily translate to net reduction in energy consumption and positive environmental outcomes. It is expected that convenience of the automated vehicles encourages the consumers to travel more, and this <a href="/wiki/Induced_demand" title="Induced demand">induced demand</a> may partially or fully offset the <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_automobiles" title="Fuel economy in automobiles">fuel efficiency</a> improvement brought by automation.<sup id="cite_ref-EEICAV_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEICAV-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Overall, the consequences of vehicle automation on global energy demand and emissions are highly uncertain, and heavily depends on the combined effect of changes in consumer behavior, policy intervention, technological progress and vehicle technology.<sup id="cite_ref-EEICAV_142-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEICAV-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By reducing the labor and other costs of <a href="/wiki/Mobility_as_a_service" title="Mobility as a service">mobility as a service</a>, automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> could reduce the number of <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> that are individually owned, replaced by taxi/pooling and other car-sharing services.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kpmg_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kpmg-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> This would also dramatically reduce the size of the automotive production industry, with corresponding environmental and economic effects.
</p><p>The lack of stressful <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b>, more productive time during the trip, and the potential savings in travel time and cost could become an incentive to live far away from cities, where housing is cheaper, and work in the city's core, thus increasing travel distances and inducing more <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">urban sprawl</a>, raising energy consumption and enlarging the <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">carbon footprint</a> of urban travel.<sup id="cite_ref-EEICAV_142-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEICAV-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sprawl_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sprawl-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> There is also the risk that traffic congestion might increase, rather than decrease.<sup id="cite_ref-EEICAV_142-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEICAV-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RAND_130-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAND-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Appropriate public policies and regulations, such as zoning, pricing, and urban design are required to avoid the negative impacts of increased suburbanization and longer distance travel.<sup id="cite_ref-RAND_130-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAND-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sprawl_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sprawl-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-parking_and_parking_space"><b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">Self</b>-parking and parking space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Self-parking and parking space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A study conducted by <a href="/wiki/AAA_Foundation_for_Traffic_Safety" title="AAA Foundation for Traffic Safety">AAA Foundation for Traffic Safety</a> found that drivers did not trust <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-parking technology, even though the systems outperformed drivers with a backup camera. The study tested <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-parking systems in a variety of vehicles (Lincoln MKC, Mercedes-Benz ML400 4Matic, Cadillac CTS-V Sport, BMW i3 and Jeep Cherokee Limited) and found that <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-parking <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> hit the curb 81% fewer times, used 47% fewer maneuvers and parked 10% faster than drivers. Yet, only 25% of those surveyed said they would trust this technology.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Manually driven vehicles are reported to be used only 4–5% of the time, and being parked and unused for the remaining 95–96% of the time.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Autonomous <a href="/wiki/Taxi" class="mw-redirect" title="Taxi">taxis</a> could, on the other hand, be used continuously after it has reached its destination. This could dramatically reduce the need for <a href="/wiki/Parking_space" title="Parking space">parking space</a>. For example, in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> a 2015 study found 14% of the land is used for parking alone, equivalent to some 1,702 hectares (4,210 acres).<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> This combined with the potential reduced need for road space due to improved traffic flow, could free up large amounts of land in urban areas, which could then be used for parks, recreational areas, buildings, among other uses; making cities more livable.
</p><p>Besides this, privately owned <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b>, also capable of <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-parking would provide another advantage: the ability to drop off and pick up passengers even in places where parking is prohibited. This would benefit <a href="/wiki/Park_and_ride" title="Park and ride">park and ride</a> facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Privacy">Privacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Privacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The vehicles' increased awareness could aid the police by reporting on illegal passenger behavior, while possibly enabling other crimes, such as deliberately crashing into another vehicle or a pedestrian.<sup id="cite_ref-Miller_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miller-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> However, this may also lead to much expanded mass surveillance if there is wide access granted to third parties to the large data sets generated.
</p><p>Privacy could be an issue when having the vehicle's location and position integrated into an interface that other people have access to.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> In addition, there is the risk of <a href="/wiki/Automotive_hacking" title="Automotive hacking">automotive hacking</a> through the sharing of information through <a href="/wiki/Vehicle-to-vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Vehicle-to-vehicle">V2V</a> (Vehicle to Vehicle) and V2I (Vehicle to Infrastructure) protocols.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> There is also the risk of terrorist attacks. <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">Self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> could potentially be loaded with explosives and used as <a href="/wiki/Car_bomb" title="Car bomb">bombs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Potential_limits_or_obstacles">Potential limits or obstacles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Potential limits or obstacles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The sort of hoped-for potential benefits from increased vehicle automation described may be limited by foreseeable challenges, such as disputes over liability,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> the time needed to turn over the existing stock of vehicles from non-automated to automated,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> and thus a long period of humans and autonomous vehicles sharing the roads, resistance by individuals to having to forfeit control of their <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> concerns about the safety of driverless in practice,<sup id="cite_ref-auto3_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> and the implementation of a legal framework and consistent global government regulations for <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Other obstacles could include de-skilling and lower levels of driver experience for dealing with potentially dangerous situations and anomalies,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> ethical problems where an automated vehicle's software is forced during an unavoidable crash to choose between multiple harmful courses of action ('the <a href="/wiki/Trolley_problem" title="Trolley problem">trolley problem</a>'),<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> concerns about making large numbers of people currently employed as drivers unemployed, the potential for more intrusive mass surveillance of location, association and travel as a result of police and intelligence agency access to large data sets generated by sensors and pattern-recognition AI, and possibly insufficient understanding of verbal sounds, gestures and non-verbal cues by police, other drivers or pedestrians.<sup id="cite_ref-technologyreview_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-technologyreview-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Autonomous_Delivery_Vehicle_Pileup.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Autonomous_Delivery_Vehicle_Pileup.jpg/220px-Autonomous_Delivery_Vehicle_Pileup.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Autonomous_Delivery_Vehicle_Pileup.jpg/330px-Autonomous_Delivery_Vehicle_Pileup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Autonomous_Delivery_Vehicle_Pileup.jpg/440px-Autonomous_Delivery_Vehicle_Pileup.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Autonomous_Delivery_Vehicle_Pileup.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Autonomous delivery vehicles stuck in one place by attempting to avoid one another.</div></div></div>
<p>Possible technological obstacles for automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> are:
</p>
<ul><li>Artificial Intelligence is still not able to function properly in chaotic inner-city environments.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>A car's computer could potentially be compromised, as could a communication system between <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autosens_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autosens-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Susceptibility of the car's sensing and navigation systems to different types of weather (such as snow) or deliberate interference, including jamming and spoofing.<sup id="cite_ref-technologyreview_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-technologyreview-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Avoidance of large animals requires recognition and tracking, and Volvo found that software suited to <a href="/wiki/Caribou" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribou">caribou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elk" title="Elk">elk</a> was ineffective with <a href="/wiki/Kangaroo" title="Kangaroo">kangaroos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Autonomous <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> may require very high-quality specialised maps to operate properly. Where these maps may be out of date, they would need to be able to fall back to reasonable behaviors.</li>
<li>Competition for the radio spectrum desired for the car's communication.<sup id="cite_ref-tampabay_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tampabay-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Field programmability for the systems will require careful evaluation of product development and the component supply chain.<sup id="cite_ref-autosens_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autosens-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Current road infrastructure may need changes for automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> to function optimally.<sup id="cite_ref-badger_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-badger-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Social challenges include:
</p>
<ul><li>Government over-regulation, or even uncertainty about potential future regulation, may delay deployment of automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> on the road.<sup id="cite_ref-law_journal_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-law_journal-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Employment – Companies working on the technology have an increasing recruitment problem in that the available talent pool has not grown with demand.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> As such, education and training by third-party organisations such as providers of online courses and <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-taught community-driven projects such as DIY Robocars<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> and Formula Pi have quickly grown in popularity, while university level extra-curricular programmes such as Formula Student Driverless<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> have bolstered graduate experience. Industry is steadily increasing freely available information sources, such as code,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> datasets<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> and glossaries<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> to widen the recruitment pool.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Potential_changes_for_different_industries">Potential changes for different industries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Potential changes for different industries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The traditional automobile industry is subject to changes driven by technology and market demands. These changes include breakthrough technological advances and when the market demands and adopts new technology quickly. In the rapid advance of both factors, the end of the era of incremental change was recognized. When the transition is made to a new technology, new entrants to the automotive industry present themselves, which can be distinguished as mobility providers such as Uber and Lyft, as well as tech giants such as <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">Nvidia</a>.  As new entrants to the industry arise, market uncertainty naturally occurs due to the changing dynamics. For example, the entrance of tech giants, as well as the alliances between them and traditional car manufacturers causes a variation in the innovation and production process of autonomous vehicles. Additionally, the entrance of mobility providers has caused ambiguous user preferences. As a result of the rise of mobility providers, the number of vehicles per capita has flatlined. In addition, the rise of the sharing economy also contributes to market uncertainty and causes forecasters to question whether personal ownership of vehicles is still relevant as new transportation technology and mobility providers are becoming preferred among consumers.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxis">Taxis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Taxis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With the aforementioned ambiguous user preference regarding the personal ownership of autonomous vehicles, it is possible that the current mobility provider trend will continue as it rises in popularity. Established providers such as Uber and Lyft are already significantly present within the industry, and it is likely that new entrants will enter when business opportunities arise.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Healthcare.2C_car_repair.2C_and_car_insurance"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare,_car_repair,_and_car_insurance">Healthcare, car repair, and car insurance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Healthcare, car repair, and car insurance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With the increasing reliance of autonomous vehicles on interconnectivity and the availability of big data which is made usable in the form of real-time maps, <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> decisions can be made much faster in order to prevent collisions.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Numbers made available by the US government state that 94% of the vehicle accidents are due to human failures. As a result, major implications for the healthcare industry become apparent. Numbers from the National Safety Council on killed and injured people on US roads multiplied by the average costs of a single incident reveal that an estimated US$500 billion loss may be imminent for the US healthcare industry when autonomous vehicles are dominating the roads. It is likely the anticipated decrease in traffic accidents will positively contribute to the widespread acceptance of autonomous vehicles, as well as the possibility to better allocate healthcare resources. As collisions are less likely to occur, and the risk for human errors is reduced significantly, the repair industry will face an enormous reduction of work that has to be done on the reparation of car frames. Meanwhile, as the generated data of the autonomous vehicle is likely to predict when certain replaceable parts are in need of maintenance, car owners and the repair industry will be able to proactively replace a part that will fail soon. This "Asset Efficiency Service" would implicate a productivity gain for the automotive repair industry.  As fewer collisions implicate less money spent on repair costs, the role of the insurance industry is likely to be altered as well. It can be expected that the increased safety of transport due to autonomous vehicles will lead to a decrease in payouts for the insurers, which is positive for the industry, but fewer payouts may imply a demand drop for insurances in general. The insurance industry may have to create new insurance models in the near future to accommodate the changes.  An unexpected disadvantage of the widespread acceptance of autonomous vehicles would be a reduction in organs available for transplant.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Rescue.2C_emergency_response.2C_and_military"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rescue,_emergency_response,_and_military">Rescue, emergency response, and military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Rescue, emergency response, and military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The technique used in autonomous <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> also ensures life savings in other industries. The implementation of autonomous vehicles with rescue, emergency response, and military applications has already led to a decrease in deaths.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Military personnel use autonomous vehicles to reach dangerous and remote places on earth to deliver fuel, food and general supplies, and even rescue people. In addition, a future implication of adopting autonomous vehicles could lead to a reduction in deployed personnel, which will lead to a decrease in injuries, since the technological development allows autonomous vehicles to become more and more autonomous. Another future implication is the reduction of emergency drivers when autonomous vehicles are deployed as fire trucks or ambulances. An advantage could be the use of real-time traffic information and other generated data to determine and execute routes more efficiently than human drivers. The time savings can be invaluable in these situations.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interior_design_and_entertainment">Interior design and entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Interior design and entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With the driver decreasingly focused on operating a vehicle, the interior design and media-entertainment industry will have to reconsider what passengers of autonomous vehicles are doing when they are on the road. Vehicles need to be redesigned, and possibly even be prepared for multipurpose usage. In practice, it will show that travelers have more time for business and/or leisure. In both cases, this gives increasing opportunities for the media-entertainment industry to demand attention. Moreover, the advertisement business is able to provide location based ads without risking driver safety.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunication_and_energy">Telecommunication and energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Telecommunication and energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>All <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> can benefit from information and connections, but autonomous <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> "Will be fully capable of operating without C-V2X."<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> In addition, the earlier mentioned entertainment industry is also highly dependent on this network to be active in this market segment. This implies higher revenues for the telecommunication industry.
</p><p>Since many autonomous vehicles are going to rely on electricity to operate, the demand for lithium batteries increases. Similarly, radar, sensors, <a href="/wiki/Lidar" title="Lidar">lidar</a>, and high-speed internet connectivity require higher auxiliary power from vehicles, which manifests as greater power draw from batteries.<sup id="cite_ref-EEICAV_142-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEICAV-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The larger battery requirement causes a necessary increase in supply of these type of batteries for the chemical industry. On the other hand, with the expected increase of battery powered (autonomous) vehicles, the petroleum industry is expected to undergo a decline in demand. As this implication depends on the adoption rate of autonomous vehicles, it is unsure to what extent this implication will disrupt this particular industry. This transition phase of oil to electricity allows companies to explore whether there are business opportunities for them in the new energy ecosystem.
</p>
<h3><span id="Restaurant.2C_hotels.2C_and_airlines"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Restaurant,_hotels,_and_airlines">Restaurant, hotels, and airlines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Restaurant, hotels, and airlines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Driver interactions with the vehicle will be less common within the near future, and in the more distant future the responsibility will lie entirely with the vehicle. As indicated above, this will have implications for the entertainment- and interior design industry. For roadside restaurants, the implication will be that the need for customers to stop <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> and enter the restaurant will vanish, and the autonomous vehicle will have a double function. Moreover, accompanied with the rise of disruptive platforms such as Airbnb that have shaken up the hotel industry, the fast increase of developments within the autonomous vehicle industry might cause another implication for their customer bases. In the more distant future, the implication for motels might be that a decrease in guests will occur, since autonomous vehicles could be redesigned as fully equipped bedrooms. The improvements regarding the interior of the vehicles might additionally have implications for the airline industry. In the case of relatively short-haul flights, waiting times at customs or the gate imply lost time and hassle for customers. With the improved convenience in future car travel, it is possible that customers might go for this option, causing a loss in customer bases for airline industry.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elderly_and_disabled">Elderly and disabled</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Elderly and disabled">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The elderly and <a href="/wiki/Persons_with_disabilities" class="mw-redirect" title="Persons with disabilities">persons with disabilities</a> (such as persons who are <a href="/wiki/Hearing-impaired" class="mw-redirect" title="Hearing-impaired">hearing-impaired</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vision_impairment" class="mw-redirect" title="Vision impairment">vision-impaired</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persons_with_reduced_mobility" title="Persons with reduced mobility">mobility-impaired</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_impairment" class="mw-redirect" title="Cognitive impairment">cognitively-impaired</a>) are potential beneficiaries of adoption of autonomous vehicles; however, the extent to which such populations gain greater mobility from the adoption of AV technology depends on the specific designs and regulations adopted.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Children">Children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Student_transport" title="Student transport">Student transport</a></div>
<p>Children and teens, who are not able to drive a vehicle themselves, are also benefiting of the introduction of autonomous <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (November 2019)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. Daycares and schools are able to come up with automated pick up and drop off systems by car in addition to <a href="/wiki/Walking" title="Walking">walking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a> and busing, causing a decrease of reliance on parents and childcare workers. The extent to which human actions are necessary for <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> will vanish. Since current vehicles require human actions to some extent, the <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> school industry will not be disrupted until the majority of autonomous transportation is switched to the emerged dominant design. It is plausible that in the distant future <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> a vehicle will be considered as a luxury, which implies that the structure of the industry is based on new entrants and a new market.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents">Incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_self-driving_car_fatalities" title="List of self-driving car fatalities">List of <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> car fatalities</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tesla_Autopilot">Tesla Autopilot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Tesla Autopilot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Autopilot" title="Tesla Autopilot">Tesla Autopilot</a></div>
<p>In mid&#x2011;October 2015, <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" class="mw-redirect" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla Motors</a> rolled out version 7 of their software in the US that included <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Autopilot" title="Tesla Autopilot">Tesla Autopilot</a> capability.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> On 9 January 2016, Tesla rolled out version 7.1 as an <a href="/wiki/Over-the-air_programming" title="Over-the-air programming">over-the-air</a> update, adding a new "summon" feature that allows <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> to <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-park at parking locations without the driver in the car.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Tesla's automated <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> features is currently classified as a Level 2 driver assistance system according to the <a href="/wiki/SAE_International" title="SAE International">Society of Automotive Engineers'</a> (SAE) five levels of vehicle automation. At this level the car can be automated but requires the full attention of the driver, who must be prepared to take control at a moment's notice.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Autopilot should be used only on <a href="/wiki/Limited-access_highway" class="mw-redirect" title="Limited-access highway">limited-access highways</a>, and sometimes it will fail to detect lane markings and disengage itself. In urban <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> the system will not read traffic signals or obey stop signs. The system also does not detect pedestrians or cyclists.<sup id="cite_ref-HwyOnly_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HwyOnly-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_Hwy_40.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tesla_Model_S_Hwy_40.jpg/230px-Tesla_Model_S_Hwy_40.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tesla_Model_S_Hwy_40.jpg/345px-Tesla_Model_S_Hwy_40.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Tesla_Model_S_Hwy_40.jpg/460px-Tesla_Model_S_Hwy_40.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2263" data-file-height="1509" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_Hwy_40.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S#Autopilot" title="Tesla Model S">Tesla Model S Autopilot system</a> in use in July 2016; it was only suitable for <a href="/wiki/Limited-access_highway" class="mw-redirect" title="Limited-access highway">limited-access highways</a>, not for urban <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b>. Among other limitations, it could not detect pedestrians or cyclists.<sup id="cite_ref-HwyOnly_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HwyOnly-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>On 20 January 2016, the first known fatal crash of a Tesla with Autopilot occurred in China's Hubei province. According to China's <a href="/wiki/163.com" class="mw-redirect" title="163.com">163.com</a> news channel, this marked "China's first accidental death due to Tesla's automatic <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> (system)". Initially, Tesla pointed out that the vehicle was so badly damaged from the impact that their recorder was not able to conclusively prove that the car had been on Autopilot at the time; however, 163.com pointed out that other factors, such as the car's absolute failure to take any evasive actions prior to the high speed crash, and the driver's otherwise good <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> record, seemed to indicate a strong likelihood that the car was on Autopilot at the time. A similar fatal crash occurred four months later in Florida.<sup id="cite_ref-china-fatality_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-china-fatality-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, in a subsequent civil suit between the father of the driver killed and Tesla, Tesla did not deny that the car had been on Autopilot at the time of the accident, and sent evidence to the victim's father documenting that fact.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The second known fatal accident involving a vehicle being driven by itself took place in <a href="/wiki/Williston,_Florida" title="Williston, Florida">Williston, Florida</a> on 7 May 2016 while a Tesla Model S <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric car</a> was engaged in Autopilot mode. The occupant was killed in a crash with an 18-wheel <a href="/wiki/Tractor-trailer" class="mw-redirect" title="Tractor-trailer">tractor-trailer</a>. On 28 June 2016 the <a href="/wiki/US_National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" class="mw-redirect" title="US National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">US National Highway Traffic Safety Administration</a> (NHTSA) opened a formal investigation into the accident working with the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Highway_Patrol" title="Florida Highway Patrol">Florida Highway Patrol</a>. According to NHTSA, preliminary reports indicate the crash occurred when the tractor-trailer made a left turn in front of the Tesla at an intersection on a non-controlled access highway, and the car failed to apply the brakes. The car continued to travel after passing under the truck's trailer.<sup id="cite_ref-AutopilotCrash01_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutopilotCrash01-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AutopilotCrash02_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutopilotCrash02-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> NHTSA's preliminary evaluation was opened to examine the design and performance of any automated <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> systems in use at the time of the crash, which involved a population of an estimated 25,000 Model S <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> On 8 July 2016, NHTSA requested Tesla Motors provide the agency detailed information about the design, operation and testing of its Autopilot technology. The agency also requested details of all design changes and updates to Autopilot since its introduction, and Tesla's planned updates schedule for the next four months.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Tesla, "neither autopilot nor the driver noticed the white side of the tractor-trailer against a brightly lit sky, so the brake was not applied." The car attempted to drive full speed under the trailer, "with the bottom of the trailer impacting the windshield of the Model S". Tesla also claimed that this was Tesla's first known autopilot death in over 130&#160;million miles (210&#160;million kilometers) driven by its customers with Autopilot engaged, however by this statement, Tesla was apparently refusing to acknowledge claims that the January 2016 fatality in Hubei China had also been the result of an autopilot system error. According to Tesla there is a fatality every 94&#160;million miles (151&#160;million kilometers) among all type of vehicles in the US<sup id="cite_ref-AutopilotCrash01_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutopilotCrash01-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AutopilotCrash02_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AutopilotCrash02-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> However, this number also includes fatalities of the crashes, for instance, of motorcycle drivers with pedestrians.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2016, the US <a href="/wiki/National_Transportation_Safety_Board" title="National Transportation Safety Board">National Transportation Safety Board</a> (NTSB) opened a formal investigation into the fatal accident while the Autopilot was engaged. The NTSB is an investigative body that has the power to make only policy recommendations. An agency spokesman said "It's worth taking a look and seeing what we can learn from that event, so that as that automation is more widely introduced we can do it in the safest way possible."<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> In January 2017, the NTSB released the report that concluded Tesla was not at fault; the investigation revealed that for Tesla <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b>, the crash rate dropped by 40 percent after Autopilot was installed.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Tesla, starting 19 October 2016, all Tesla <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> are built with hardware to allow full <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> capability at the highest safety level (SAE Level 5).<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> The hardware includes eight surround cameras and twelve ultrasonic sensors, in addition to the forward-facing radar with enhanced processing capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> The system will operate in "shadow mode" (processing without taking action) and send data back to Tesla to improve its abilities until the software is ready for deployment via over-the-air upgrades.<sup id="cite_ref-geuss_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geuss-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> After the required testing, Tesla hopes to enable full <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> by the end of 2020 under certain conditions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Waymo">Waymo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Waymo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Google_driverless_car_at_intersection.gk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Google_driverless_car_at_intersection.gk.jpg/220px-Google_driverless_car_at_intersection.gk.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Google_driverless_car_at_intersection.gk.jpg/330px-Google_driverless_car_at_intersection.gk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Google_driverless_car_at_intersection.gk.jpg/440px-Google_driverless_car_at_intersection.gk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1490" data-file-height="990" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Google_driverless_car_at_intersection.gk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Google's in-house <a href="/wiki/Waymo" title="Waymo">automated car</a></div></div></div>
<p>Waymo originated as a <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> car project within <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>. In August 2012, Google announced that their vehicles had completed over 300,000 automated-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> miles (500,000&#160;km) accident-free, typically involving about a dozen <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> on the road at any given time, and that they were starting to test with single drivers instead of in pairs.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> In late-May 2014, Google revealed a new prototype that had no steering wheel, gas pedal, or brake pedal, and was fully automated .<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> As of March&#160;2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Google had test-driven their fleet in automated mode a total of 1,500,000&#160;mi (2,400,000&#160;km).<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> In December 2016, Google Corporation announced that its technology would be spun off to a new company called Waymo, with both Google and Waymo becoming subsidiaries of a new parent company called <a href="/wiki/Alphabet_Inc." title="Alphabet Inc.">Alphabet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Google's accident reports as of early 2016, their test <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> had been involved in 14 collisions, of which other drivers were at fault 13 times, although in 2016 the car's software caused a crash.<sup id="cite_ref-WashingtonPost_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonPost-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2015, Brin confirmed that 12 vehicles had suffered collisions as of that date. Eight involved rear-end collisions at a stop sign or traffic light, two in which the vehicle was side-swiped by another driver, one in which another driver rolled through a stop sign, and one where a Google employee was controlling the car manually.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> In July 2015, three Google employees suffered minor injuries when their vehicle was rear-ended by a car whose driver failed to brake at a traffic light. This was the first time that a collision resulted in injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> On 14 February 2016 a Google vehicle attempted to avoid sandbags blocking its path. During the maneuver it struck a bus. Google stated, "In this case, we clearly bear some responsibility, because if our car hadn't moved, there wouldn't have been a collision."<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> Google characterized the crash as a misunderstanding and a learning experience. No injuries were reported in the crash.<sup id="cite_ref-WashingtonPost_222-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonPost-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uber">Uber</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Uber">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 2017, an Uber test vehicle was involved in a crash in <a href="/wiki/Tempe,_Arizona" title="Tempe, Arizona">Tempe, Arizona</a> when another car failed to yield, flipping the Uber vehicle. There were no injuries in the accident.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 22 December 2017, Uber had completed 2&#160;million miles (3.2&#160;million kilometers) in automated mode.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 March 2018, <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Elaine_Herzberg" title="Death of Elaine Herzberg">Elaine Herzberg</a> became the first pedestrian to be killed by a <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> car in the United States after being hit by an Uber vehicle, also in Tempe. Herzberg was crossing outside of a <a href="/wiki/Pedestrian_crossing" title="Pedestrian crossing">crosswalk</a>, approximately 400 feet from an intersection.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> This marks the first time an individual outside an auto-piloted car is known to have been killed by such a car.
</p><p>The first death of an essentially uninvolved third party is likely to raise new questions and concerns about the safety of automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> in general.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> Some experts say a human driver could have avoided the fatal crash.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> Arizona Governor <a href="/wiki/Doug_Ducey" title="Doug Ducey">Doug Ducey</a> later suspended the company's ability to test and operate its automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> on public roadways citing an "unquestionable failure" of the expectation that Uber make public safety its top priority.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> Uber has pulled out of all <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b>-car testing in California as a result of the accident.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> On 24 May 2018 the US National Transport Safety Board issued a preliminary report.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Navya_automated_bus_driving_system">Navya automated bus <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Navya automated bus driving system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 9 November 2017, a <a href="/wiki/Navya_SAS" title="Navya SAS">Navya</a> automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> bus with passengers was involved in a crash with a truck. The truck was found to be at fault of the crash, reversing into the stationary automated bus. The automated bus did not take evasive actions or apply <a href="/wiki/Defensive_driving" title="Defensive driving">defensive <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b></a> techniques such as flashing its headlights, or sounding the horn. As one passenger commented, "The shuttle didn't have the ability to move back. The shuttle just stayed still."<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Policy_implications">Policy implications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Policy implications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_planning">Urban planning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Urban planning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to a <a href="/wiki/Wonkblog" title="Wonkblog">Wonkblog</a> reporter, if fully automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> become commercially available, they have the potential to be a <a href="/wiki/Disruptive_innovation" title="Disruptive innovation">disruptive innovation</a> with major implications for society. The likelihood of widespread adoption is still unclear, but if they are used on a wide scale, policy makers face a number of unresolved questions about their effects.<sup id="cite_ref-badger_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-badger-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>One fundamental question is about their effect on travel behavior. Some people believe that they will increase car ownership and car use because it will become easier to use them and they will ultimately be more useful.<sup id="cite_ref-badger_178-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-badger-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> This may, in turn, encourage urban sprawl and ultimately total private vehicle use. Others argue that it will be easier to share <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> and that this will thus discourage outright ownership and decrease total usage, and make <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> more efficient forms of transportation in relation to the present situation.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Policy-makers will have to take a new look at how infrastructure is to be built and how money will be allotted to build for automated vehicles. The need for traffic signals could potentially be reduced with the adoption of <a href="/wiki/Smart_highway" title="Smart highway">smart highways</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> Due to smart highways and with the assistance of smart technological advances implemented by policy change, the dependence on <a href="/wiki/Oil_dependence" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil dependence">oil imports</a> may be reduced because of less time being spent on the road by individual <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> which could have an effect on policy regarding energy.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> On the other hand, automated vehicles could increase the overall number of <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> on the road which could lead to a greater dependence on oil imports if smart systems are not enough to curtail the impact of more vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> However, due to the uncertainty of the future of automated vehicles, policy makers may want to plan effectively by implementing infrastructure improvements that can be beneficial to both human drivers and automated vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> Caution needs to be taken in acknowledgment to <a href="/wiki/Public_Transportation" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Transportation">public transportation</a> and that the use may be greatly reduced if automated vehicles are catered to through policy reform of infrastructure with this resulting in job loss and increased <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other disruptive effects will come from the use of automated vehicles to carry goods. <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">Self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> vans have the potential to make home deliveries significantly cheaper, transforming retail commerce and possibly making hypermarkets and supermarkets redundant. As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/US_Department_of_Transportation" class="mw-redirect" title="US Department of Transportation">US Department of Transportation</a> defines automation into six levels, starting at level zero which means the human driver does everything and ending with level five, the automated system performs all the <b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> tasks. Also under the current law, manufacturers bear all the responsibility to <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-certify vehicles for use on public roads. This means that currently as long as the vehicle is compliant within the regulatory framework, there are no specific federal legal barriers in the US to a highly automated vehicle being offered for sale. <a href="/wiki/Iyad_Rahwan" title="Iyad Rahwan">Iyad Rahwan</a>, an associate professor in the <a href="/wiki/MIT_Media_Lab" title="MIT Media Lab">MIT Media Lab</a> said, "Most people want to live in a world where <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> will minimize casualties, but everyone wants their own car to protect them at all costs." Furthermore, industry standards and best practice are still needed in systems before they can be considered reasonably safe under real-world conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Researchers have pushed against this arguing that <b style="color:#000;background:#ffff66">self</b>-<b style="color:#000;background:#66ffff">driving</b> <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b> will have a deeply negative impact on urban life especially if they are programmed to kill. Moreover, they require a sensor-based infrastructure that would constitute an all-encompassing surveillance apparatus.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>
They would also exasperate existing mobility inequalities<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> driven by the interests of car companies and technology companies while taking investment away from more equatable and sustainable mobility initiatives such as public transportation.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislation">Legislation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Legislation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 1968 <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Convention_on_Road_Traffic" title="Vienna Convention on Road Traffic">Vienna Convention on Road Traffic</a>, subscribed to by over 70 countries worldwide, establishes principles to govern traffic laws. One of the fundamental principles of the convention has been the concept that a <a href="/wiki/Driver_(person)" class="mw-redirect" title="Driver (person)">driver</a> is always fully in control and responsible for the behavior of a vehicle in traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> The progress of technology that assists and takes over the functions of the driver is undermining this principle, implying that much of the groundwork must be rewritten.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_status_in_the_United_States">Legal status in the United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Legal status in the United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Self_Driving_Cars_Legalized_States_in_USA.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Self_Driving_Cars_Legalized_States_in_USA.png/220px-Self_Driving_Cars_Legalized_States_in_USA.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Self_Driving_Cars_Legalized_States_in_USA.png/330px-Self_Driving_Cars_Legalized_States_in_USA.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Self_Driving_Cars_Legalized_States_in_USA.png/440px-Self_Driving_Cars_Legalized_States_in_USA.png 2x" data-file-width="1752" data-file-height="1235" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Self_Driving_Cars_Legalized_States_in_USA.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>US states that allow testing of autonomous vehicles on public roads as of June&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In the United States, a non-signatory country to the Vienna Convention, state vehicle codes generally do not envisage—but do not necessarily prohibit—highly automated vehicles as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Self-driving_car&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> To clarify the legal status of and otherwise regulate such vehicles, several states have enacted or are considering specific laws.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> By 2016, seven states (Nevada, California, Florida, Michigan, Hawaii, Washington, and Tennessee), along with the <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia" class="mw-redirect" title="District of Columbia">District of Columbia</a>, have enacted laws for automated vehicles. Incidents such as the first fatal accident by Tesla's Autopilot system have led to discussion about revising laws and standards for automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b>.
</p><p>In September 2016, the <a href="/wiki/National_Economic_Council_(United_States)" title="National Economic Council (United States)">US National Economic Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/US_Department_of_Transportation" class="mw-redirect" title="US Department of Transportation">US Department of Transportation</a> released federal standards that describe how automated vehicles should react if their technology fails, how to protect passenger privacy, and how riders should be protected in the event of an accident. The new federal guidelines are meant to avoid a patchwork of state laws, while avoiding being so overbearing as to stifle innovation.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Nevada_Legislature" title="Nevada Legislature">Nevada Legislature</a> passed a law to authorize the use of automated <b style="color:#000;background:#ffcc99">cars</b>. Nevada thus became the first jurisdiction in the world where automated vehicles might be legally operated on public roads.
